Jamison Brereton

140
Agni
D─лrghatamas Aucathya
13 verses: jagat─л, except jagat─л or triс╣гс╣нubh 10, triс╣гс╣нubh 12тАУ13
This first hymn in the D─лrghatamas cycle is bristling with difficulties in detail, although it remains focused on its central topic, the kindling and spread of the fire. The first two verses establish the ritual scene, with the ritual fire sitting on (or at) the vedi, the тАЬaltarтАЭ that is really a dug-out depression in the ground on the axis between the eastern and western ritual fires, and with the poetтАЩs presentation of his тАЬthoughtтАЭ (a praise hymn) as clothing for the ritual fire. But natural fire, which spreads through the woods and devours them, is also referred to, especially in verse 2.314 I.140
The chronological description of the kindling and growth of fire begins in verse 3 with a vivid depiction of the kindling sticks and the first faint stirrings of smoke and fire. The growing power of the fire and the swiftness of the spread of its flames, imagined as horses in verse 4, occupy the next verses (4тАУ10). FireтАЩs burning of the plants that stoke it is given an erotic cast in verses 6тАУ8, aided by the fact that several words for тАЬplantтАЭ are feminine in gender. Their very destruction by fire is also envi
sioned as a transformation into a better and more vigorous form (see esp. vss. 7cdтАУ8). The prayers for aid and material goods begin in verse 10, on behalf not only of a generic тАЬusтАЭ but especially mentioning our patrons (vss. 10, 12) and others of our circle (vs. 12). One striking request is for a metaphorical boat to deliver us to the far shore of difficulty (vs. 12); the boat is described in some detail, including its possession of a foot or feet. We wonder if this refers to some sort of primitive keel or centerboard, which would probably be helpful to ensure that the boat make it across the current of a swift-flowing river. Unfortunately our knowledge of ancient Indian naval architecture is not sufficient to decide.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬPrepare a (fit) plural ce, as it were an offering, for the radiant Agni, who is seated on the altar, and fond of his station; strew the sacred, light-bearing, bright and gloom-dispelling (spot), with agreeable (ku┼Ыa grass), as with a garment.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

To him sitting on the altar, the very bright one whose domain is dearтАФto Agni bear forth his womb like a wellspring (of nourishment).
As if with a garment, clothe the blazing one with a thoughtтАФthe
smiter of darkness whose chariot is of light, whose color is blazing bright.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The referent of dh─Бs├н- ordinarily тАШwellspringтАЩ (see comm. I.62.3), which is identified here as AgniтАЩs y├│ni- тАШwombтАЩ, is unclear. In VIII.43.7, 29 and III.7.3 (also perhaps III.7.1) the dh─Бs├н- is the plants (=firewood) to be тАЬeaten,тАЭ i.e., burned, by the fire, hence the source (тАШwellspringтАЩ) of the fireтАЩs growth. Since whatever it is here can be carried (pr├б bhar─Б), firewood makes sense, and this interpr. is supported by the fact that the plants that Agni burns are an important theme in this hymn (vss. 2ab, 6-8). Though in I.122.13, a passage adduced by Witzel Got┼Н, I render dh─Бs├н- as тАШgushтАЩ (developing a different aspect of тАШwellspring, fountainтАЩ; cf. also VI.67.6), that sense does not work well here because it must be identified with the y├│ni- and capable of being carried.

Griffith

To splendid Agni seated by the altar, loving well his home, I bring the food as ’twere his place of birth.
I clothe the bright One with my hymn as with a robe, him with the car of light, bright-hued, dispelling gloom.

Oldenberg

For him who sits on the Vedi (i. e. on the sacrificial bed), whose foundations are pleasant, for the brilliant Agni bring forward 1 a receptacle 2, which is to him like a drink. Clothe 1 the bright one in prayer as in a garment, him whose chariot is light, whose colour is bright, the destroyer of darkness.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬ(Agni), the two-fold genitive rated, devours the triple (sacrificial) food, and when the year expires renovates what has been eaten; the showerer (of benefits) is invigorated (inone form), by eating with the tongue of another; in a different form the restrainer (of) all consumes the forest trees.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Two-fold genitive rated: either as produced by attrition from the two sticks, or first by attrition and second by consecration for sacrificial use; triple-food: trivс╣Ыd-annam; 1. clarified butter; 2. puroс╕Н─Б┼Ыa butter, with other articles or cakes fried in butter; and 3. soma; renovates what has been eaten: same articles are offered annually; consumes the forest trees: anyasya-─Бs─Б jihvay─Б jenyo vс╣Ыс╣г─Бnyanyena-mс╣Ыс╣гс╣нa = liс╣н, the victorious showerer by the mouth-tongue of another; by another consumes. ─Бs─Б = asyena, with the mouth;

Anyasya = of the oblation, or with the mouth in one form (or sacrificial fire) he receives the oblation through the tongue of another, i.e. the ladle of the ministering priest; in another form, i.e., the fire that burns forests, d─Бv─Бgni, he consumes the trees

Jamison Brereton

Having two births, he stretches toward the threefold food. In a year what was eaten (by him) has grown again.
With the mouth and the tongue of one (of his forms) he is a
thoroughbred bull; with the other he drags down the trees (like) an
elephant.

Jamison Brereton Notes

I take trivс╣Ы╠Бt as a qualifier of ├бnnam тАШfoodтАЩ (so also Renou, Oldenberg [SBE], S─Бyaс╣Зa, Witzel Got┼Н); however, I am not sure what tripartition of food is meant. Geldner in his n. (2a) suggests wood, ghee, and soma (more or less flg. S─Бyaс╣Зa), but because the next p─Бda concerns only the plant food that Agni has eaten and that regenerates in a year, I am reluctant to divide the focus. It is also possible to take trivс╣Ы╠Бt as an adverb, as Geldner does (тАЬтАж eilt dreif├дltig тАжтАЭ), but this merely transfers the problem.

In the second hemistich тАЬthe one / the otherтАЭ are easier to identify. P─Бda c concerns the ritual fire, while d treats the wild fire, each represented by a characteristic animal: in c the тАЬthoroughbred bullтАЭ (j├йnyo vс╣Ы╠Бс╣г─Б), which, despite its power, is a domesticated beast, while the (wild) elephant (v─Бraс╣З├бс╕е) of d rampages in the forest.

I donтАЩt understand the position of ─л: ─л(m) and s─лm generally occupy WackernagelтАЩs position. In this case it may mark jagdh├бm as a notional relative clause, as in my tr. тАЬwhat was eaten,тАЭ though the following word p├║naс╕е unfortunately must be construed with the main verb v─Бvс╣Ыdhe.

In c the initial position of any├бsya violates my rule (1997, Fs. Beekes) for definite any├б- placement, but any├йna in d is correctly positioned.

Griffith

Child of a double birth he grasps at triple food; in the year’s course what he hath swallowed grows anew.
He, by another’s mouth and tongue a noble Bull, with other, as an elephant, consumes the trees.

Oldenberg

He who has a twofold birth 1, presses on towards the threefold food 2; what he has eaten grows again after a year 3. With the mouth and the tongue of the one he (shows himself as) the noble, manly one; with the other (mouth) the stubborn (Agni) wipes off the trees 4.

Geldner

Der Zweigeborene eilt dreif├дltig auf die Speise los. In Jahresfrist w├дchst wieder, was er verzehrt hat. Mit dem Munde, der Zunge des einen ist er der h├дusliche Stier, mit dem anderen zieht der Elefant die B├дume hernieder.

Grassmann

Der zwiegeborne greift nach dreierlei Genuss, im Lauf des Jahres w├дchst das aufgezehrte wieder neu; Mit anderm Mund und Zunge zehrt aufs neue er, der edle Stier, der m├дchtige die B├дume auf.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬBoth his associated mothers, blackened (by combustion), are in movement, and give birth to an infant, whose tongue (of flame glows) in the east; (who) dissipates darkness; (who) rapidly issues forth; (who) is readily developed; (who) is (ever) to be cherished, and is the augmenter (of the prosperity) of his parent, (the instrumental tutor of the rite).тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Plunging into the black, jerking back and forth, both his mothers [=kindling sticks], sharing the same abode, move athwart each other toward their childтАФ
to him, producing smoke, his tongues stretching forward, stirring
thirstily, quivering, worthy to be attended upon, the increaser of his father [=priest].

Jamison Brereton Notes

The middle voice of tarete, fairly rare for forms of тИЪtс╣Э, is responsible for my тАЬmove athwart each other,тАЭ against a more standard тАЬhasten towardsтАЭ or the like. It is also a reasonable representation of the movement of the kindling sticks rubbing against each other.

On тИЪdhvaс╣Гs see comm. ad IV.19.7.

Both s─Б╠Бcya and k├║paya- are hapaxes, though the likely root affiliation of the former with тИЪsac тАШaccompany, attend uponтАЩ makes its interpr. easier. With AiG II.2.793, 798, I take it to be a gerundive to this root. As for k├║paya-, I find it hard to separate it from the root тИЪkup тАШquiver, quakeтАЩ, despite the unclarity of its formation (suffix? accent?), and find the alternative analysis as ku-paya(s?)- (most recently, tentatively Witzel Got┼Н) unlikely.

v├бrdhanam pit├║с╕е тАЬthe increaser of his fatherтАЭ is one of the RVic poetтАЩs beloved paradoxes. The priest generates the ritual fire and is therefore its father, but the well-tended fire in turn produces prosperity and increase for the ritual officiants.

Griffith

The pair who dwell together, moving in the dark bestir themselves: both parents hasten to the babe,
Impetuous-tongued, destroying, springing swiftly forth, one to be watched and cherished, strengthener of his sire.

Oldenberg

Both his mothers 1, dwelling together, immersed in darkness, and affrighted, proceed towards the young child who stretches forward his tongue, who sparkling moves about thirstily, whom men should attach to themselves, who agitates (the world), the increaser of his father 2.

Die Schwarzantilopen h├╝pfend, zitternd, laufen sich seine beiden beisammen wohnenden M├╝tter um das Kind ab, das die Zunge vorstreckt, Funken stiebt, gierig, sich bewegt, um den Pflegling, den ……, den F├╢rderer seines Vaters.

Zu ihrem Sohne gehn erschreckt die Aeltern hin, die mit ihm wohnen, die im Dunkel wallenden; Zu ihm, der z├╝ngelnd spr├╝ht, dem gierig eilenden, dem gern man dient, der flackernd seinen Vater labt.

рд╡реНрдпрд╛рдкрдирд╢реАрд▓рд╛рдГ рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThe (flames of Agni), light-moving, dark-tracked, quick (consuming), capricious, restless, plural ying lightly, fanned by the wind, wide-spreading, and ensuring liberation (to the devout), are kindled for (the benefit of) the pious reverencer of (holy) priests.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

‘Flames of Agni’ is inserted to explain the epithets: raghu-druvaс╕е, going lightly; kс╣Ыс╣гс╣Зas─лt─Бsaс╕е, black-pathed; juvaс╕е, quick; asaman─Б, not same-minded (some going east, some west or in different colours); ajir─Бsaс╕е, moving; raghuс╣гyadaс╕е, light-gliding; v─Бtaj┼лtaс╕е, wind-impelled; ─Б┼Ыavaс╕е, pervading; mumukс╣гvaс╕е, giving liberation

Jamison Brereton

For Manu and the offspring of Manu to come they are harnessedтАФthe speedy (horses) seeking to break free, running fast, drawing black furrows, quick, racing fast, breaking ranks, sped by the wind, swift.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The thrust of this vs. is a pile-up of adjectives describing AgniтАЩs flamehorses, set within a frame consisting of the verb ├║pa yujyante тАЬthey are harnessed,тАЭ postponed until the final p─Бda, and a dative of benefit occurring in the first: m├бnave m─Бnavasyat├й.

m─Бnavasyat├й is found only here, and both its sense and its formation are unclear. It is generally rendered as if it were a denominative (Geldner тАШdem MenschenfreundlichenтАЩ, Renou тАШagissant en hommeтАЩ), but this would assume a -y├бformation built to a vс╣Ыddhi-derivative pseudo-s-stem *m─Бnavas- (beside m─Бnav├б-, loosely like m├бnus- beside m├бnu-). I instead interpret it as a (pseudo-)future participle in -sy├бnt- built to the common vс╣Ыddhi deriv. m─Бnava-. The future suffix reinforces the sense of the vс╣Ыddhi deriv. тАШdescending from ManuтАЩ by emphasizing the fact that (some of) these descendants are still to come. (If such a derivation seems too radical, it could be mediated by a denom. *m─Бnava-y├б- + -sy├бnt-, which underwent haplology.) asaman├б- means lit. something like тАШnot together, not gatheredтАЩ; тАШbreaking ranksтАЩ seems a dynamic tr. of the underlying concept (Renou тАШallant en sens diversтАЩ).

(See also VII.5.3.) It thus forms a semantic pair with mumukс╣гv├ас╕е тАШseeking to break freeтАЩ in a. I do not follow Geldner (/Witzel Got┼Н) in their derivation from the extended meaning of s├бmana- as тАШbattleтАЩ, hence (Geldner) тАШohne KampfтАЩ.

Note the phonetic figure opening the vs.: mumukс╣гv├▓ m├бnave m─Бnavasyat├й.

Griffith

For man, thou Friend of men, these steeds of thine are yoked, impatient, lightly running, ploughing blackened lines,
Discordant-minded, fleet, gliding with easy speed, urged onward by the wind and rapid in their course.

Oldenberg

Thy speedy (teams) 1 that strive to break loose for the benefit of the man who acts as men do, the swift ones, drawing black furrows-thy quick (horses), striving apart, the agile, swift runners, incited by the wind, are yoked.

Geldner

Dem Menschenfreundlichen werden die schnellf├╝├Яigen Rennstuten angeschirrt, die dem Menschen durchgehen wollen, die schwarze Furchen ziehen, die behenden auch ohne Kampf schnellaufend, wie windgetriebene Renner.

Grassmann

Dem menschengleichen Gotte werden angeschirrt die fl├╝cht’gen Renner, die nach Freiheit trachtenden, Die auseinanderstrebend schwarze Furchen ziehn, die windschnell eilen raschen Laufes, raschen Flugs.

Elizarenkova

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдпрдГ

рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдп: рдпреЗ рдореБрдореБрдХреНрд╖реНрд╡рд╕реНрддреЗ рдпрдерд╛ рд░рдШреБрджреНрд░реБрд╡реЛ рдЬреБрд╡реЛрд╜рд╕рдордирд╛ рдЕрдЬрд┐рд░рд╛рд╕реЛ рд░рдШреБрд╕реНрдпрджреЛ рд╡рд╛рддрдЬреВрддрд╛ рдЖрд╢рд╡рдГ рдХреГрд╖реНрдгрд╕реАрддрд╛рд╕рдГ рдХреГрд╖реАрд╡рд▓рд╛рдГ рдХреГрд╖рд┐рдХрд░реНрдордгреНрдпреБрдкрдпреБрдЬреНрдпрдиреНрддреЗ рддрдерд╛ рдорд╛рдирд╡рд╕реНрдпрддреЗ рдордирд╡реЗ рд╡рд┐рджреБрд╖реЗ рдпреЛрдЧрд┐рди рдЙрдкрдпреБрдЬреНрдпрдиреНрддрд╛рдореН рее рек рее

рдЖрддреН рдЕрдирдиреНрддрд░рдореН рдЕрд╕реНрдп рд╕реНрддреВрдпрдорд╛рдирд╕реНрдпрд╛рдЧреНрдиреЗ рддреЗ рдкреНрд░рд╕рд┐рджреНрдзрд╛ рд╡рд┐рд╕реНрдлреБрд▓рд┐рдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдГ рд╡реГрдерд╛ рд╕рд╣реИрд╡ рдИрд░рддреЗ рд╕рд░реНрд╡рддреЛ рдЧрдЪреНрдЫрдиреНрддрд┐ ред рдХреАрджреГрд╢рд╛рд╕реНрддреЗ ред рдзреНрд╡рд╕рдпрдиреНрддрдГ рддрдорд╛рдВрд╕рд┐ рдзреНрд╡рдВрд╕рдпрдиреНрддрдГ рддрдерд╛ рдХреГрд╖реНрдгрд╡рд░реНрдгрдореН рдЕрднреНрд╡рдВ рдорд╣рд╛рдиреНрддрдорднрд┐рднрд╡рджреНрдЧрдордирдорд╛рд░реНрдЧрдВ рдорд╣рд┐ рдорд╣рддреН рд╡рд░реНрдкрдГ рд░реВрдкрдВ рдкреНрд░рдХрд╛рд╢рдВ рдХрд░рд┐рдХреНрд░рддрдГ рдЕрддреНрдпрд░реНрдердВ рдХреБрд░реНрд╡рдиреНрддрдГред рдХрд╕реНрдорд┐рдиреН рдХрд╛рд▓реЗ рдЗрддрд┐ рддрджреБрдЪреНрдпрддреЗ ред рдпрддреН рдпрджрд╛ рдорд╣реАрдВ рдорд╣рддреАрдореН рдЕрд╡рдирд┐рдВ рднреВрдорд┐рдВ рд╕реАрдВ рд╕рд░реНрд╡рддрдГ рдорд░реНрдореГрд╢рддреН рдкреБрдирдГрдкреБрдирд░рд╛рдореГрд╢рддреН рее рдореГрд╢реЗрд░реНрдпрдЩрд▓реБрдЧрдиреНрддрд╛рддреН рд╢рддрд░рд┐ тАШрдЕрднреНрдпрд╕реНрддрд╛рдирд╛рдорд╛рджрд┐рдГ’ рдЗрддреНрдпрд╛рджреНрдпреБрджрд╛рддреНрддрддреНрд╡рдореН рее рдЕрднрд┐рд╢реНрд╡рд╕рди рд╕рд░реНрд╡рддрд╢реНрдЪреЗрд╖реНрдЯрдорд╛рдирдГ рд╕реНрддрдирдпрдиреН рд╢рдмреНрджрдВ рдХреБрд░реНрд╡рдиреН рдирд╛рдирджрддреН рдЕрддреНрдпрд░реНрдердВ рд╢рдмреНрджрдпрдиреН рее рдкреВрд░реНрд╡рд╡рддреН рдкреНрд░рддреНрдпрдпрд╕реНрд╡рд░реМ рее рдЕрднрд┐рддрдГ рдкреНрд░рдХрд░реНрд╖реЗрдг рдПрддрд┐ рдЧрдЪреНрдЫрддрд┐ ред рдпрджрд╛ рдЗрддрд╕реНрддрддреЛ рдЬрд┐рд╣реНрд╡рд╛рднрд┐рд░реНрд▓реЗрд▓рд┐рд╣рд╛рдиреЛ рднреБрдЧреБрднреБрдЧреБрдзреНрд╡рдирд┐рдВ рдХреБрд░реНрд╡рдиреН рдЬреНрд╡рд▓рддрд┐ рддрджреИрд╡ рд╡рд┐рд╕реНрдлреБрд▓рд┐рдЩреНрдЧрд╛ рдЙрджреНрднрд╡рдиреНрддреАрддреНрдпрд░реНрдердГ рее рее рел рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThereupon those (flames of Agni) extend together in all directions, dispersing gloom, and spreading great light along the path of darkness; when (Agni) illumines repeatedly the whole earth, and proceeds panting thundering, and roaring aloud.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

After that do these (flames) of his, producing smoke, rise at will, making and remaking a black void and a great form,
while he goes forth, stroking the great (earth) as his streambed, snorting, thundering, constantly roaring.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The vs. contains three тАЬintensiveтАЭ participles: k├бrikrataс╕е, m├бrmс╣Ы┼Ыat, and n─Б╠Бnadat. All three, in my opinion, express repetitive or repeated action. In particular k├бrikrataс╕е, in my tr. тАШmaking and remakingтАЩ, nicely reflects the constantly changing shape of the smoke rising from the raging flames.

I take mah─л╠Бm тАШgreatтАЩ (fem.) separately from av├бnim and referring to the earth; by this interpr. the whole earth serves as AgniтАЩs course (тАШstream bedтАЩ).

Griffith

Dispelling on their way the horror of black gloom, making a glorious show these flames of his fly forth,
When o’er the spacious tract he spreads himself abroad, and rushes panting on with thunder and with roar.

Oldenberg

When he stroking his wide course proceeds panting, thundering, roaring, then those sparkling (rays) of his fly about wildly, displaying wondrous darkness, a large sight 1.

Geldner

Dann brechen ausgelassen seine Flammen hervor, Funken stiebend, indem sie das schwarze Ungeheuer, die gro├Яe Gestalt hervorwirbeln. Wenn er zupackend, anschnaubend, donnernd, laut br├╝llend seine , m├дchtige Bahn zieht.

Grassmann

Dann steigen spielend seine spr├╝h’nden Flammen auf, wenn schwarzes Graun und grosse Pracht er wechselnd schafft, Wenn kr├дftig er die grosse Himmelsbahn durchstreicht, wenn schnaufend, donnernd er und laut erdr├╢hnend geht.

Elizarenkova

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдЬреЛ рдордиреБрд╖реНрдп рдЗрд╕ рд╕рдВрд╕рд╛рд░ рдореЗрдВ рд╢рд░реАрд░ рдХрд╛ рдЖрд╢реНрд░рдп рдХрд░ рдЕрдзрд░реНрдо рдХрд░рддреЗ рд╣реИрдВ, рд╡реЗ рджреГрдврд╝ рдмрдиреНрдзрди рдХреЛ рдкрд╛рддреЗ рд╣реИрдВ рдФрд░ рдЬреЛ рд╢рд╛рд╕реНрддреНрд░реЛрдВ рдХреЛ рдкрдврд╝, рдпреЛрдЧрд╛рднреНрдпрд╛рд╕ рдХрд░, рдзрд░реНрдо рдХрд╛ рдЕрдиреБрд╖реНрдард╛рди рдХрд░рддреЗ, рдЙрдиреНрд╣реАрдВ рдХреА рдореБрдХреНрддрд┐ рд╣реЛрддреА рд╣реИ рее рел рее

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - (рдЖрддреН) рдЖрдирдиреНрддрд░реНрдпреЗ (рдЕрд╕реНрдп) (рддреЗ) (рдзреНрд╡рд╕рдпрдиреНрддрдГ) рдзреНрд╡рд╕рдорд┐рд╡рд╛рдЪрд░рдиреНрддрдГ (рд╡реГрдерд╛) рдорд┐рдереНрдпрд╛ (рдИрд░рддреЗ) (рдХреГрд╖реНрдгрдореН) рд╡рд░реНрдгрдореН (рдЕрднреНрд╡рдореН) рдЕрднрд╡рдиреНрддрдореН (рдорд╣рд┐) рдорд╣рддреН (рд╡рд░реНрдкрдГ) (рдХрд░рд┐рдХреНрд░рддрдГ) рдпреЗрд╜рддрд┐рд╢рдпреЗрди рдХреБрд░реНрд╡рдиреНрддрд┐ (рдпрддреН) рдпреЗ (рд╕реАрдореН) рд╕рд░реНрд╡рддрдГ (рдорд╣реАрдореН) рдорд╣рддреАрдореН (рдЕрд╡рдирд┐рдореН) рдкреГрдерд┐рд╡реАрдореН (рдкреНрд░) (рдЕрднрд┐) (рдорд░реНрдореГрд╢рддреН) рдЕрддрд┐рд╢рдпреЗрди рд╕рд╣рдорд╛рдирдГ (рдЕрднрд┐рд╢реНрд╡рд╕рдиреН) рд╕рд░реНрд╡рддрдГ рд╢реНрд╡рд╕рдиреНрдкреНрд░рд╛рдгрдВ рдзрд░рдиреН (рд╕реНрддрдирдпрдиреН) рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпреБрджрд┐рд╡ рд╢рдмреНрджрдпрдиреН (рдПрддрд┐) рдЧрдЪреНрдЫрддрд┐ (рдирд╛рдирджрддреН) рдЕрддрд┐рд╢рдпреЗрди рдирд╛рджрдВ рдХреБрд░реНрд╡рдиреН рее рел рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬHe stoops down among the bushes as if embellishing them (with his lustre), and rushes roaring like a bull amongst (a herd of) cows; thence increasing in intensity, he enhances (the fierceness) of his form, and is difficult to be arrested as a formidable (animal), when he brandishes his horns. Like a bull amongst: vс╣Ыс╣гeva pantir abhyeti; patnir = p─Бlayitr─лс╕е, those who cherish him, Agni, i.e., bushes, timber; patn─л = a cow].тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

He who, like a busy attendant, keeps bending over the brown (females [=plants])тАФhe goes toward (them) like a bull to his wives, constantly bellowing. And, showing his power, he beautifies their [?] bodies. Like a fearsome (bull), the one difficult to grasp keeps shaking his horns.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The concentration of intensives continues in this verse: n├бmnate (a), r├│ruvat (b), davidh─Бva (d).

The тАШbendingтАЩ of p─Бda a of course describes the flickering motion of the flames.

Because of the theme mentioned ad vss. 6-8, of the bodily transformation of the plants by burning, I take tanv├аs in c as referring to the bodies of the plants, not, with most tr., that of Agni.

I donтАЩt entirely understand the position of ca in c. Klein (DGRV I.222-23, 259-60) suggests that it has been bumped by the participle opening the clause and p─Бda. It is certainly the case that ca could not immediately follow that first word without metrical distress: five-syllable oj─Бy├бm─Бnaс╕е entirely fills the opening, and since the caesura cannot precede an enclitic, placing ca after the participle would result in an opening of 6.

Jamison Brereton Notes

This trio of verses treats the union (by burning) of the hyper-masculine Agni/fire and the plants (feminine). This must be the тАЬder erotische GrundtonтАЭ of the hymn that Geldner mentions in his introduction. This sexual union leads to the death of the plants (8b) and their regrowth and transformation into a different form (7cd, 8). Or so is my interpr.; acdg. to some, the flames are sometimes the referents, rather than the plants.

This proposed split reference seems to me to break the thematic unity of the verses and the climax in 8 of the death and renewed life of the females who unite with Agni.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬNow hidden, now displayed, he seizes (on the fuel), as if understanding (the purpose of the worshipper), and even reposes amidst the conscious (flames); again they break forth, and repair to the divine (fire of sacrifice), blending with which they give a different (luminous)form to their parents, (heaven and earth).тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

He masses together those spread asunder and those close-packed [=plants]. Recognizing the (females) just as they recognize him, he
lies in his own (place).
They grow again; they approach divinity. They make for themselves a form different from their parents, (though) in company with them.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The idiom punar тИЪvс╣Ыdh тАШgrow againтАЩ recurs from 2b, again referring to the plants immolated by the fire (at least in my opinion; others take the subject to be the flames). Here their regeneration is linked with their contact or merger with divinity.

The final p─Бda is variously interpreted. I take the plants still to be the subject and the form тАЬdifferent from their parentsтАЭ refers to their burned residue as ash and cinders, as opposed to the branches and leaves that were fed to the fire. But if pitr├│с╕е is taken as a loc., the referent may be different; some take it as referring to Heaven and Earth (S─Бyaс╣Зa, Oldenberg [SBE], Witzel Got┼Н).

06-08 ...{Loading}...
Jamison Brereton Notes

This trio of verses treats the union (by burning) of the hyper-masculine Agni/fire and the plants (feminine). This must be the тАЬder erotische GrundtonтАЭ of the hymn that Geldner mentions in his introduction. This sexual union leads to the death of the plants (8b) and their regrowth and transformation into a different form (7cd, 8). Or so is my interpr.; acdg. to some, the flames are sometimes the referents, rather than the plants.

This proposed split reference seems to me to break the thematic unity of the verses and the climax in 8 of the death and renewed life of the females who unite with Agni.

Griffith

Now covered, now displayed he grasps as one who knows his resting-place in those who know him well.
A second time they wax and gather Godlike power, and blending both together change their Parents’ form.

Oldenberg

He clasps (the plants, &c.) that have been laid together and have been laid out 1. Knowing them, while they know him, and being their own (friend or lover) he lies on them. They grow again and attain godhead. They produce together another shape of the parents 2.

Geldner

Die engstehenden und die weitstehenden erfasst er. Als Bekannter liegt er bei Bekannten als rechtm├д├Яiger Gatte. Sie wachsen wieder und gehen in der g├╢ttlichen Wesenheit auf. Bei den Eltern nehmen sie eine andere Gestalt an.

Grassmann

Die sich vereinen und zerstreuen, h├дlt er fest, vertraut auf die vertrauten legt er dauernd sich, Sie wachsen wieder und erlangen Gotteskraft, und andres Ansehn schaffen ihren Aeltern sie.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThe curving tresses (of the flames) embrace him, (Agni), and when expiring spring aloft again to (greet) their coming (lord); rescuing them from decrepitude, he comes sounding aloud, genitive rating (in them) intenser animation and unimpaired vitality.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

The curving tresses: agruva ke┼Ыin─лс╕е;

Agruvaс╕е = fingers, as an attributive, implies either those that are in front, agrataс╕е sthitaс╕е, or crooked or curved like fingers

Jamison Brereton

For the long-haired spinsters embrace him; despite having died, they stand erect (to go) forth once again for ─Аyu [=Agni?].
Removing their old age, he goes constantly roaring, generating a
further living life-force (for them?), which cannot be laid low.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Again there is a difference of opinion as to referent. With Oldenberg (SBE) I take the plants once again as the subjects of p─Бda a (so, partly, Witzel Got┼Н), contra S─Бyaс╣Зa, Geldner, Renou, K├╝mmel (419), who interpret them as flames.

06-08 ...{Loading}...
Jamison Brereton Notes

This trio of verses treats the union (by burning) of the hyper-masculine Agni/fire and the plants (feminine). This must be the тАЬder erotische GrundtonтАЭ of the hymn that Geldner mentions in his introduction. This sexual union leads to the death of the plants (8b) and their regrowth and transformation into a different form (7cd, 8). Or so is my interpr.; acdg. to some, the flames are sometimes the referents, rather than the plants.

This proposed split reference seems to me to break the thematic unity of the verses and the climax in 8 of the death and renewed life of the females who unite with Agni.

Griffith

The maidens with long, tresses hold him in embrace; dead, they rise up again to meet the Living One.
Releasing them from age with a loud roar he comes, filling them with new spirit, living, unsubdued.

Oldenberg

The long-haired virgins 1 have embraced him. Having died they stand upright again for him (Agni) the living one (or, for him the ├Вyu). Delivering them of old age he proceeds roaring, procreating another vital spirit, an indestructible life.

Geldner

Denn ihn halten die langhaarigen Unverm├дhlten umfasst; schon gestorben haben sie sich f├╝r den Langlebigen wieder aufgerichtet. Das Alter von ihnen nehmend kommt er br├╝llend, h├╢heren Geist, unverw├╝stliches Leben erzeugend.

Grassmann

Die Jungfraun, die langhaar’gen, halten ihn umfasst, die todten sind erstanden neu dem lebenden, Ihr Alter l├╢send geht er brausend, zeugend nun lebend’gen Odem, bessern, unbezwinglichen.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬLicking up the (verdant) vesture of the mother (of all things, earth), the rapid (Agni) proceeds with resounding existences; granting sustenance to (every) footed (creature); ever consuming (fuel), so that a blackened track follows (hispath).тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Proceeds with resounding existences: tuvigrebhiс╕е satvabhiс╕е viy─Бti = he goes variously with living beings, sounding loudly, or going quickly, accompanied by the cries or the flight of animals when he sets fire to a forest;

Footed: padvate = to that which has feet, either bipeds or quadrupeds

Jamison Brereton

Licking all around his motherтАЩs [=earthтАЩs] over-garment, he drives across the expanse with his powerfully spirited warriors,
producing vigor for the footed, while licking and licking always. The white (track of ash) follows along his tracks.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The hapax tuvigr├б- in b is generally interpr. as having a thematized form of тИЪgс╣Э тАШswallowтАЩ as 2nd member, hence тАШpowerfully swallowingтАЩ vel sim. But to a seс╣н root we should probably expect *-gira- (like -t├нr-: -tira-; (-)t├║r-: t├║ra-). I follow instead a suggestion of InslerтАЩs, that it represents a haplologized *tuvi-vigr├б- тАШpowerfully spiritedтАЩ.

With most, I take ┼Ыy├йn─л as the fem. of the color term ┼Ыyet├б-, rather than, with Geldner, as the fem. of ┼Ыyen├б- тАШfalconтАЩ (Adlerweibchen). Among other things, we would probably expect the fem. of тАШfalconтАЩ to have vс╣Ыk─л╠Б- inflection, like vс╣Ыk─л╠Б- itself and siс╣Гh─л╠Б- тАШlionessтАЩ to siс╣Гh├б- тАШlionтАЩ; it should therefore have suffixal accent, and in this sandhi context the nom. sg. should have come out as *┼Ыyen─л╠Бс╕е. Moreover there is no obvious role for a female falcon in context. The white trail of ash here contrasts nicely with the black furrows (kс╣Ыс╣гс╣З├бs─лta-) the fire creates in 4b.

Griffith

Licking the mantle of the Mother, far and wide he wanders over fields with beasts that flee apace.
Strengthening all that walk, licking up all around, a blackened path, forsooth, he leaves where’er he goes.

Oldenberg

Licking everywhere the upper garment of the mother 1, he spreads himself over the space with his mightily devouring warriors, giving strength to everything that has feet, licking and licking. The reddish white one 2 follows her ways 3.

Das Obergewand der Mutter Erde rings beleckend nimmt er mit den lautschreienden Kriegern seinen Lauf querdurch, dem was F├╝├Яe hat, St├дrkung schaffend, immer hin und her leckend. - Das Adlerweibchen folgt seinen Bahnen nach.

Grassmann

Und seiner Mutter Oberkleid beleckend rings durchl├дuft die Flur er mit den starken, gierigen, Kraft gebend dem, was F├╝sse hat, und leckend stets; die Morgenr├╢the folget seinen Bahnen nach.

рд╣реЗ рдЕрдЧреНрдиреЗ рдЕрд╕реНрдорд╛рдХрдВ рдордШрд╡рддреНрд╕реБ рдЕрд╕реНрдорддреНрд╕рдВрдмрдиреНрдзрд┐рд╖реБ рдЕрдиреНрдирд╡рддреНрд╕реБ рдпрд╛рдЧреЗрд╖реБ рдЧреГрд╣реЗрд╖реБ рд╡рд╛ рджреАрджрд┐рд╣рд┐ рджреАрдкреНрдпрд╕реНрд╡ ред рдЕрдз рдЕрдерд╛рдирдиреНрддрд░рдВ рд╢реНрд╡рд╕реАрд╡рд╛рдиреН рд╢реНрд╡рд╕рдирд╡рд╛рдиреН рдЬреНрд╡рд╛рд▓рд╛рднрд┐рд╢реНрдЪреЗрд╖реНрдЯрд╡рд╛рдиреН рдЕрд╕реНрдорд╕реНрдкреНрд░рд╛рдгрдирд╡рд╛рдиреН рд╡рд╛ рд╡реГрд╖рднрдГ рд╡рд░реНрд╖рд┐рддрд╛ рдЕрднрд┐рдорддрд╛рдирд╛рдВ рджрдореВрдирд╛рдГ рджрд╛рдирдордирд╛ рджрдордордирд╛ рджрд╛рдиреНрддрдордирд╛ рд╡рд╛ рд╕рд░реНрд╡рддреНрд░ рднрд╡реЗрддрд┐ рд╢реЗрд╖рдГ ред рд╕ рдЙрдХреНрддрд▓рдХреНрд╖рдгрд╕реНрддреНрд╡рдВ рд╢рд┐рд╢реБрдорддреАрдГ рдЕрд╡рд╛рд╕реНрдп ред рд╢рд┐рд╢реБрд╢рдмреНрджреЗрди рддрджрд╡рд╕реНрдерд╛ рд▓рдХреНрд╖реНрдпрддреЗ ред рд╢реИрд╢рд╡рд╡рддреАрд░реНрдЬреНрд╡рд╛рд▓рд╛ рдЕрдкрдХреНрд╖реЗрдкреНрдп рд╡рд┐рд╣рд╛рдп рдЕрджреАрджреЗрдГ рднреГрд╢рдВ рджреАрдкреНрдпрд╕реНрд╡ ред рдХреАрджреГрд╢рд╕реНрддреНрд╡рдореН ред рдпреБрддреНрд╕реБ рд╕рдВрдЧреНрд░рд╛рдореЗрд╖реБ рд╡рд░реНрдореЗрд╡ рдХрд╡рдЪрдорд┐рд╡ рдкрд░рд┐рдЬрд░реНрднреБрд░рд╛рдгрдГ рдЕрд╕реНрдорджреНрджреНрд╡реЗрд╖реНрдЯреДрдиреН рдкреБрдирдГрдкреБрдирдГ рдкрд░рд┐рд╣рд░рдиреН ред рдпрджреНрд╡рд╛ ред рдпреБрддреНрд╕реБ рд╕рдВрдЧреНрд░рд╛рдореЗрд╖реБ рд╡рд░реНрдореЗрд╡ рдкрд░рд┐рдЬрд░реНрднреБрд░рд╛рдгреЛ рднрд╡ рее рд╣рд╕реНрддреЗрд░реНрдпрдЩреНрд▓реБрдЧрдиреНрддрд╛рддреН рд╡реНрдпрддреНрдпрдпреЗрди рд╢рд╛рдирдЪреН ред тАШрдЕрднреНрдпрд╕реНрддрд╛рдирд╛рдорд╛рджрд┐рдГ’ рдЗрддреНрдпрд╛рджреНрдпреБрджрд╛рддреНрддрддреНрд╡рдореН рее рдЙрдХреНрддрдЧреБрдгрдХреЛ рднрд╡ рдордШрд╡рддреНрд╕реБ рдпрдЬреНрдЮреЗрд╖реБ рджреАрдкреНрдпрд╕реНрд╡ рее рее рем рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬShine, Agni, in our opulent (abodes), vivifying, showering (blessings), bounteous, casting off infantine (glimmerings); blaze (fiercely), repelling repeatedly, like a coat of mail, (our enemies) in combats.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Shine upon our bounteous (patrons), o Agni. Then as the snorting bull, the master of the household,
*having set loose the females who have young [=flames], you have
shone, ever flickering and enveloping like armor in battles.

Jamison Brereton Notes

I read p─Бda b with cd, contrary to the standard tr., which take it as independent. I might, however, replace the tr. of ├бdha as тАШthenтАЩ with тАШandтАЩ or the like.

The first word of c, av─Б╠Бs i ya, is generally taken as the gerund to ├бva тИЪas lit.

тАШthrow downтАЩ. I am dubious about this interpr., since that lexeme is not found elsewhere in the RV or, acdg. to Monier Williams, anywhere else in Sanskrit. I therefore derive it rather from ├бva тИЪs─Б / si тАШlet loose, unhitchтАЩ, despite the formal difficulties. The idiom is used regularly for letting loose horses, to which AgniтАЩs flames are compared here, and see X.61.20, where Agni is the subject of ├бva syati, a verse that contains vocabulary that resonates here: dvivartan├н- and ┼Ы├н┼Ыu-. The problem is that we should expect avas─Б╠Бya with full-grade root and root accent (cf. I.104.1) or possibly *avasi y├а (this zero-gr. form is recorded in WhitneyтАЩs Roots). I can only explain the accented long vowel in av─Б╠Бs i ya as arising from confusion produced by augmented forms (cf. ├бv─Бsuс╕е тАШthey unhitchedтАЩ I.179.2).

I take the ┼Ы├н┼Ыumat─лс╕е тАШ(females) possessing youngтАЩ to be AgniтАЩs flames; they have young because flames beget more flames as they spread.

I take d as a paradox: the fire is in constant circling motion (parij├бrbhur─Бс╣Зaс╕е), but still produces a protective encirclement like armor.

Griffith

O Agni, shine resplendent with our wealthy chiefs, like a loud-snorting bull, accustomed to the house.
Thou casting off thine infant wrappings blazest forth as though thou hadst put on a coat of mail for war.

Oldenberg

Shine, O Agni, among our liberal lords, for thou art a mightily breathing bull, a friend of the house. Throwing down the (mothers) of the young child 1 thou hast shone, (a protector of thy friends) like a coat of mail in battles, hurrying around.

Geldner

Bei unserem Lohnherren leuchte, o Agni, und sei der Hausgebieter, du der schnaubende Stier! Die M├╝tter absto├Яend leuchtest du auf, wie ein Panzer in den Schlachten hin und her funkelnd.

Grassmann

O Agni, leuchte unsern Opferherren hell, und m├дchtig schnaufend wie ein Stier ans Haus gew├╢hnt,Die samenreichen niederlegend strahltest du hellfunkelnd, wie ein Panzer in den Schlachten gl├дnzt.

рд╣реЗ рдЕрдЧреНрдиреЗ рдЗрджрдореН рдЕрд╕реНрдорджреАрдпрдВ рд╕реЛрдорд╛рджрд┐рд░реВрдкрдВ рд╣рд╡рд┐рдГ ред рдХреАрджреГрд╢рдВ рддрддреН ред рджреБрд░реНрдзрд┐рддрд╛рддреН рджреБрд╖реНрдЯрдВ рд╕реНрдерд╛рдкрд┐рддрд╛рддреН рдХрдард┐рдирд╛рддреН рдХрд╛рд╖реНрдард╛рджреЗрдГ рдЕрдзрд┐ рдЙрдкрд░рд┐ рд╕реБрдзрд┐рддрдВ рд╕реБрд╣рд┐рддрдВ рд╕реБрд╖реНрдареБ рджрддреНрддрдореН ред рдордиреНрдордирдГ рдордирдиреАрдпрд╛рддреН рдкреНрд░рд┐рдпрд╛рджреБ рдЪрд┐рддреН рддрд╡ рд╣реГрджреНрдпрд╛рджрдкрд┐ ред рдЙрд╢рдмреНрджреЛрд╜рд╡рдзрд╛рд░рдгреЗ ред рдЪрд┐рдЪреНрдЫрдмреНрджреЛрд╜рдкрд┐рд╢рдмреНрджрд╛рд░реНрдердГ ред рддреЗ рддрд╡ рдкреНрд░реЗрдпрдГ рдЕрддрд┐рдкреНрд░рд┐рдпрддрдордореН рдЕрд╕реНрддреБ ред рддрддреНрдХрд┐рдорд┐рддреНрдпрд╛рд╣ ред рд╣реЗ рдЕрдЧреНрдиреЗ рддреЗ рддрд╡ рддрдиреНрд╡рдГ рд╢рд░реАрд░рд╕реНрдп рдШреГрддреЗрдиреЛрдЬреНрдЬреНрд╡рд▓рд┐рддрд╛рдпрд╛ рдЬреНрд╡рд╛рд▓рд╛рдпрд╛рдГ рд╢реБрдЪрд┐ рдирд┐рд░реНрдорд▓рдВ рд╢реБрдХреНрд░рдВ рджреАрдкреНрддрдВ рдпрддреН рддреЗрдЬрдГ рд░реЛрдЪрддреЗ рддреЗрди рд╕рд╣ рд░рддреНрдирдВ рд░рдордгреАрдпрдВ рдордгрд┐рдореБрдХреНрддрд╛рджрд┐рдХрдВ рд╡рд┐рддрд░рдиреН рдЕрд╕реНрдорднреНрдпрдВ рд╡рдирд╕реЗ рдЕрд╕реНрдорд╛рдиреН рд╕рдВрднрдЬрд╕реНрд╡ рее рд╡рдирддреЗрд░реНрд╡реНрдпрддреНрдпрдпреЗрдирд╛рддреНрдордиреЗрдкрджрдореН рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬMay this oblation, Agni, carefully plural ced upon the rugged but agreeable (pile of fuel), be most acceptable to you, so that the pure radiance of your person n may shine brightly, and you may grant us wealth.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Let this well-formed (thought) be dearer to you than one poorly formed, o Agni, and dearer to you even than your own dear thought. With what of your body shines blazing bright you will win treasure for us.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Most take the expression in b to mean тАЬlet it be dearer to you than a dear thoughtтАЭ; this seems to me nonsensical or at least rhetorically weak. I suggest that there is a pun on priy├б-, which can mean both тАШdearтАЩ and тАШownтАЩ. Here the poet suggests that his composed thought will be dearer to Agni than anything the god himself might produce.

Griffith

May this our perfect prayer be dearer unto thee than an imperfect prayer although it please thee well.
With the pure brilliancy that radiates from thy form, mayest thou grant to us abundant store of wealth.

Oldenberg

May this well-composed (prayer), O Agni, be more welcome to thee than a badly-composed oneтАФmore welcome than even a welcome prayer. With the bright light of thy body win thou treasures for us.

Geldner

Dieses wohlgeratene Gedicht soll dir mehr als ein schlechtgeratenes, lieber noch selbst als ein liebes Gedicht sein, o Agni. Was Helles, Reines an deinem K├╢rper gl├дnzt, damit gewinnst du f├╝r uns das Kleinod.

Grassmann

Dies sch├╢n beschaffne sei, o Agni, lieber dir als schlechtes Opfer, ja auch als ein liebes Lied; Was leuchtend dir von deinem Leibe hell erstrahlt, mit dem gew├дhre du uns reiche Kostbarkeit.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬBestow, Agni, upon our exfellent patron a boat ever fitted with oars and feet, (one that may render) our posterity prosperous, and may bear mankind across (the ocean of life) to felicity.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Upon our excellent patron: rath─Бya no gс╣Ыh─Бya = lit. to our carriage-house; rath─Бya, an adjective for raс╣Еhan─Бya, agreeable; gс╣Ыha, a house (applies to the yajam─Бna, as the asylum of the needy, or of the priests); a boat ever fitted: n─Бvam nity─Бritr─Бm padvat─лm; the boat is explained by yaj├▒a the sacrifice, the oars are the priests, the materials are the fuel and apparatus and the feet are the divinities, the prayers, and offerings.

Jamison Brereton

For our chariot and for our house, o Agni, give us a boat with built-in oars and a foot [=keel? rudder?],
which will carry our heroes and our bounteous (patrons) and our
peoples to the further shore and which (will be) our shelter.

Jamison Brereton Notes

See published introduction. for speculation on the тАЬfootтАЭ of the boat.

Geldner suggests persuasively that тАЬchariot and houseтАЭ are used metaphorically for (times of) war and peace.

Griffith

Grant to our chariot, to our house, O Agni, a boat with moving feet and constant oarage,
One that may further well our wealthy princes and all the folk, and be our certain refuge.

Oldenberg

Grant us, Agni, for our chariot and for our house a ship which has its own rudders and which has feet 1, which may save our strong men and our liberal lords and our people, and which may be a shelter for us.

Geldner

Gew├дhre, Agni, unserem Wagen und Haus ein Schiff mit eigenen Rudern und mit F├╝├Яen, das unsere Mannen und unsere Lohnherren und die Leute hin├╝bertrage und das eine Zuflucht sei.

Grassmann

Gib, Agni, unserm Wagen, unserm Hause das Schiff, das selbst sich rudert und beweget, Das unsre Helden ├╝berf├дhrt, die F├╝rsten und alles Volk, und sichre Zuflucht bietet.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬAgni, be propitiated by this our earnest praise, and may heaven and earth, and the spontaneously-flowing (streams), provide for us the produce of the herd, and of the field; and may the purple coursers (of the dawn) bestow upon us abundant food through a length of days.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

O Agni, may you welcome just our recitation, (as may) heaven and earth, and the rivers, which sing their own praises
as they go toward an abundance of cattle and of grain through the
long days. The ruddy (dawns/cattle?) will choose refreshment as their boon (for us?).

Jamison Brereton Notes

The problem in this verse is to determine which p─Бdas go together. Geldner and Renou construe ab and cd together, but this leads to a gender problem: the subj. of cd should be fem. pl. aruс╣Зy├ас╕е in d, but c contains a nom. pl. masc. part. y├бntaс╕е. (Oldenberg [SBE] suggests that this form is corrupt because of the metrical problems in the p─Бda; he treats these at length in Noten, but does not seem to favor emendation of the participle.) The problem is not entirely solved by taking c with (a)b, as Oldenberg (SBE) and I do, but it becomes somewhat attenuated by the variety of possible subjects: Agni (m.), Heaven and Earth (dy─Б╠Бv─Б-kс╣г─Б╠Бm─Б, dual dvandva, whose gender is listed by Grassmann as fem., but there are no diagnostic passages), the rivers (s├нndhu-, sometimes fem., sometimes masc. [see common acc. pl. s├нndh┼лn]) – with masc. prevailing either because masc. is the default in such gender clashes or because s├нndhavaс╕е is the closest subject to y├бntaс╕е. Witzel Got┼Н also take d with the nominatives of b, by somehow taking aruс╣Зy├ас╕е as a temporal expression тАЬbei den (Morgen)r├╢ten,тАЭ but one would expect a loc. for this meaning (as opposed to the extent of time in the temporal d─лrgh─Б╠Бh─Б тАЬthrough the long daysтАЭ of c).

Griffith

Welcome our laud with thine approval, Agni. May earth and heaven and freely flowing rivers
Yield us long life and food and corn and cattle, and may the red Dawns choose for us their choicest.

Oldenberg

Approve, O Agni, our hymn alone. May Heaven and Earth and the Rivers, delightful by their own nature 1, going their way 2, (choose for us) bliss in cows and crops, long days; may the red (Dawns) choose food for us as a choice boon.

Geldner

Unser Preislied m├╢gest du Agni, beif├дllig aufnehmen, Himmel und Erde und die Fl├╝sse, die ihr eigenes Lob singen. Die Morgenr├╢ten um Rind- und Kornreichtum angehend, um lange Lebenstage, bitten sie sich Speisegenu├Я als Lohngabe aus.

Grassmann

Du nimm, o Agni, freundlich unser Lied an, und Erd’ und Himmel und erfreut die Str├╢me; Sie m├╢gen wandernd Rind und Korn und Alter die Morgenr├╢then Trunk und Schatz uns spenden.

Elizarenkova

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдЗрд╕ рдордиреНрддреНрд░ рдореЗрдВ рд╡рд╛рдЪрдХрд▓реБрдкреНрддреЛрдкрдорд╛рд▓рдЩреНрдХрд╛рд░ рд╣реИред рдордиреБрд╖реНрдпреЛрдВ рдХреЛ рд╕рджрд╛ рдкреБрд░реБрд╖рд╛рд░реНрдереА рд╣реЛрдирд╛ рдЪрд╛рд╣рд┐рдпреЗ, рдЬрд┐рди рдпрд╛рдиреЛрдВ рд╕реЗ рднреВрдорд┐, рдЕрдиреНрддрд░рд┐рдХреНрд╖, рд╕рдореБрджреНрд░ рдФрд░ рдирджрд┐рдпреЛрдВ рдореЗрдВ рд╕реБрдЦ рд╕реЗ рд╢реАрдШреНрд░ рдЬрд╛рдирд╛ рд╣реЛ, рдЙрди рдпрд╛рдиреЛрдВ рдкрд░ рдЪрдврд╝рдХрд░ рдкреНрд░рддрд┐рджрд┐рди рд░рд╛рддреНрд░рд┐ рдХреЗ рдЪреМрдереЗ рдкреНрд░рд╣рд░ рдореЗрдВ рдЙрдардХрд░ рдФрд░ рджрд┐рди рдореЗрдВ рди рд╕реЛрдпрдХрд░ рд╕рджрд╛ рдкреНрд░рдпрддреНрди рдХрд░рдирд╛ рдЪрд╛рд╣рд┐рдпреЗ, рдЬрд┐рд╕рд╕реЗ рдЙрджреНрдпрдореА рдРрд╢реНрд╡рд░реНрдп рдХреЛ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрдд рд╣реЛрддреЗ рд╣реИрдВ рее резрей реердЗрд╕ рд╕реВрдХреНрдд рдореЗрдВ рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рд╛рдиреЛрдВ рдХреЗ рдкреБрд░реБрд╖рд╛рд░реНрде рдФрд░ рдЧреБрдгреЛрдВ рдХрд╛ рд╡рд░реНрдгрди рд╣реЛрдиреЗ рд╕реЗ рдЗрд╕ рд╕реВрдХреНрдд рдХреЗ рдЕрд░реНрде рдХреА рдкрд┐рдЫрд▓реЗ рд╕реВрдХреНрдд рдХреЗ рдЕрд░реНрде рдХреЗ рд╕рд╛рде рд╕рдЩреНрдЧрддрд┐ рд╣реИ, рдпрд╣ рдЬрд╛рдирдирд╛ рдЪрд╛рд╣рд┐рдпреЗ реердпрд╣ рдПрдХрд╕реМ рдЪрд╛рд▓реАрд╕рд╡рд╛рдБ рд╕реВрдХреНрдд рдФрд░ рд╕рд╛рддрд╡рд╛рдБ рд╡рд░реНрдЧ рд╕рдорд╛рдкреНрдд рд╣реБрдЖ рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдпрдГ

рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдп: рдпрдерд╛ рджреНрдпрд╛рд╡рд╛рдХреНрд╖рд╛рдорд╛ рд╕рд┐рдиреНрдзрд╡реЛрд╜рд░реБрдгреНрдпрд╢реНрдЪ рд╡рд░рдорд┐рд╖рдореБрдХреНрдердВ рдЧрд╡реНрдпрдВ рдпрд╡реНрдпрдВ рдпрдиреНрддрдГ рд╕реНрд╡рдЧреВрд░реНрддреНрддрд╛рдГ рд╕рдиреНрддрдГ рджреАрд░реНрдШрд╛рд╣рд╛рд╡рд░рдиреНрдд рддрдерд╛рдЧреНрдиреЗ рдиреЛрд╜рднреАрдЬреНрдЬреБрдЧреБрд░реНрдпреНрдпрд╛рдГ рее резрей рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдГ

рдкреБрдирд╕реНрддрдореЗрд╡ рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдорд╛рд╣ ред

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - (рдЕрднрд┐) рдЖрднрд┐рдореБрдЦреНрдпреЗред рдЕрддреНрд░ рд╕рдВрд╣рд┐рддрд╛рдпрд╛рдорд┐рддрд┐ рджреАрд░реНрдШрдГред (рдирдГ) рдЕрд╕реНрдорд╛рдиреН (рдЕрдЧреНрдиреЗ) рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рдиреН (рдЙрдХреНрдердореН) рдкреНрд░рд╢рдВрд╕рдиреАрдпрдореН (рдЗрддреН) (рдЬреБрдЧреБрд░реНрдпрд╛рдГ) рдЙрджреНрдпрдЪреНрдЫреЗрдГред рдЙрджреНрдпрдорд┐рдирдГ рдХреБрд░реНрдпрд╛рдГ (рджреНрдпрд╛рд╡рд╛рдХреНрд╖рд╛рдорд╛) рдЕрдиреНрддрд░рд┐рдХреНрд╖рдВ рднреВрдорд┐рд╢реНрдЪ (рд╕рд┐рдиреНрдзрд╡рдГ) рд╕рдореБрджреНрд░рд╛ рдирджреНрдпрд╢реНрдЪ (рдЪ) (рд╕реНрд╡рдЧреВрд░реНрддреНрддрд╛рдГ) рд╕реНрд╡реИрд░реБрджреНрдпрддрд╛рдГ (рдЧрд╡реНрдпрдореН) рдЧреЛрд░реНрд╡рд┐рдХрд╛рд░рдВ рджреБрдЧреНрдзрд╛рджрд┐рдХрдВ рд╕реБрд╡рд░реНрдгрд╛рджрд┐рдХрдВ рд╡рд╛ (рдпрд╡реНрдпрдореН) рдпрд╡рд╛рдирд╛рдВ рднрд╡рдирдВ рдХреНрд╖реЗрддреНрд░рдореН (рдпрдиреНрддрдГ) рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрдиреБрд╡рдиреНрддрдГ (рджреАрд░реНрдШрд╛) рджреАрд░реНрдШрд╛рдгрд┐ (рдЕрд╣рд╛) рджрд┐рдирд╛рдирд┐ (рдЗрд╖рдореН) рдЕрдиреНрдирдореН (рд╡рд░рдореН) рд░рддреНрдирд╛рджрд┐рдХрдореН (рдЕрд░реБрдгреНрдпрдГ) рдЙрд╖рдГрдХрд╛рд▓рд╛ (рд╡рд░рдиреНрдд) рд╕реНрд╡реАрдХреБрд░реНрдпреБрдГред рдЕрддреНрд░ рд╡реНрдпрддреНрдпрдпреЗрди рд╢рдкреН рее резрей рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдЕрддреНрд░ рд╡рд╛рдЪрдХрд▓реБрдкреНрддреЛрдкрдорд╛рд▓рдЩреНрдХрд╛рд░рдГред рдордиреБрд╖реНрдпреИрдГ рд╕рджрд╛ рдкреБрд░реБрд╖рд╛рд░реНрдерд┐рднрд┐рд░реНрднрд╡рд┐рддрд╡реНрдпрдВ рдпреИрд░реНрдпрд╛рдиреИрдГ рднреВрдореНрдпрдиреНрддрд░рд┐рдХреНрд╖рд╕рдореБрджреНрд░рдирджреАрд╖реБ рд╕реБрдЦреЗрди рдЧрдордирдВ рд╕реНрдпрд╛рддреНрддрд╛рдирд┐ рдпрд╛рдирд╛рдиреНрдпрд╛рд░реБрд╣реНрдп рдкреНрд░рддрд┐рджрд┐рдирдВ рд░рдЬрдиреНрдпрд╛рд╢реНрдЪрддреБрд░реНрдереЗ рдкреНрд░рд╣рд░ рдЙрддреНрдерд╛рдп рджрд┐рд╡рд╕реЗрд╜рд╕реБрдкреНрддреНрд╡рд╛ рд╕рджрд╛ рдкреНрд░рдпрддрд┐рддрд╡реНрдпрдВ рдпрдд рдЙрджреНрдпрдорд┐рди рдРрд╢реНрд╡рд░реНрдпрдореБрдкрдпрдиреНрддреНрдпрдд рдЗрддрд┐ рее резрей реердЕрддреНрд░ рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рддреНрдкреБрд░реБрд╖рд╛рд░реНрдердЧреБрдгрд╡рд░реНрдгрдирд╛рджреЗрддрддреНрд╕реВрдХреНрддрд╛рд░реНрдерд╕реНрдп рдкреВрд░реНрд╡рд╕реВрдХреНрддрд╛рд░реНрдереЗрди рд╕рд╣ рд╕рдЩреНрдЧрддрд┐рд░рд╕реНрддреАрддрд┐ рд╡реЗрджреНрдпрдореН реердЗрддрд┐ рдЪрддреНрд╡рд╛рд░рд┐рдВрд╢рджреБрддреНрддрд░рдВ рд╢рддрддрдордВ рд╕реВрдХреНрддрдВ рд╕рдкреНрддрдореЛ рд╡рд░реНрдЧрд╢реНрдЪ рд╕рдорд╛рдкреНрддрдГ рее

рд╕рд╡рд┐рддрд╛ рдЬреЛрд╢реА тЖР рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рдо) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдпрд╛ рдордВрддреНрд░рд╛рдд рд╡рд╛рдЪрдХрд▓реБрдкреНрддреЛрдкрдорд╛рд▓рдВрдХрд╛рд░ рдЖрд╣реЗ. рдорд╛рдгрд╕рд╛рдВрдиреА рдиреЗрд╣рдореА рдкреБрд░реБрд╖рд╛рд░реНрдереА рд╡реНрд╣рд╛рд╡реЗ. рдЬреНрдпрд╛ рдпрд╛рдирд╛рдВрдиреА рднреВрдореА, рдЕрдВрддрд░рд┐рдХреНрд╖, рд╕рдореБрджреНрд░ рд╡ рдирджреНрдпрд╛рддреВрди рд╕реБрдЦрд╛рдиреЗ рдЬрд▓рдж рдЬрд╛рддрд╛ рдпреЗрдИрд▓ рдЕрд╢рд╛ рдпрд╛рдирд╛рдВрддреВрди рджрд░рд░реЛрдЬ рд░рд╛рддреНрд░реАрдЪреНрдпрд╛ рдЪреМрдереНрдпрд╛ рдкреНрд░рд╣рд░реА рдЙрдареВрди рджрд┐рд╡рд╕рд╛ рди рдЭреЛрдкрддрд╛ рд╕рджреИрд╡ рдкреНрд░рдпрддреНрди рдХреЗрд▓рд╛ рдкрд╛рд╣рд┐рдЬреЗ рдЬреНрдпрд╛рдореБрд│реЗ рдРрд╢реНрд╡рд░реНрдп рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрдд рд╡реНрд╣рд╛рд╡реЗ рее резрей рее
